<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Trustees Decemr 15. 1856. Adjourned Meeting '> Trustees <date when='1856-12-15'>Decem<sup>r</sup> 15. 1856.</date> Adjourned Meeting </span></p>
<p>A meeting of the Trustees was held according to <span class='line-break'> </span>the aforesaid adjournment, at the usual place, <date when='1856-12-15T18:00:00'>on Monday <span class='line-break'> </span>Evening, December 15<sup>th</sup> at 6 o'clock</date>. ~</p>
<p>There were present, <a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->the President</a>, and Messrs <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/62841' title='Cheever, James'>Cheever</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/62842' title='Crocker, Uriel'>Crocker</a><a href='/pages/subjects/54774' title='Little, Charles C.'>, Little,</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/62843' title='McKean, Henry S.'>McKean</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54820' title='Nazro, Charles G.'>Nazro</a> &amp; <a href='/pages/subjects/54952' title='Tisdale, Mace'>Tisdale</a>. _</p>
<p>The report of the Committee upon By-Laws was</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279280">
<h3><a name="page-1279280">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 113)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>113</p>
<p>taken up by special assignment and read: - <span class='line-break'> </span>Several articles were reconsidered and amended.<span class='line-break'> </span>The last article, upon "Alteration of By Laws was <span class='line-break'> </span>adopted, and the entire Code was then passed. - -</p>
<p>The votes recommended in the second paragraph <span class='line-break'> </span>of the report were passed. - - The meeting was then adjourned.</p>
<p>Attest  <a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'>Austin J. Coolidge</a>, Secretary.</p>
<p>The following is a copy of the Report, including <span class='line-break'> </span>the Code of By-Laws. - -</p>
<p>The Committee appointed to prepare a Code <span class='line-break'> </span>of By-Laws respectfully report: -</p>
<p>That with the assistance of the Secretary they have examined <span class='line-break'> </span>the Records of the Corporation and Trustees, and have selected<span class='line-break'> </span>therefrom such standing votes as appeared to them to require in- <span class='line-break'> </span>corporation into the proposed Code of By-Laws. They have endeavored<span class='line-break'> </span>to arrange, condense and simplify said votes so as to make them <span class='line-break'> </span>intelligible and convenient of reference.  They have omitted some <span class='line-break'> </span>things which appeared to them superfluous, and have introduced <span class='line-break'> </span>others which they considered essential to the connexion and <span class='line-break'> </span>completeness of the Code.</p>
<p>If the Code now reported shall be adopted, they recommend <span class='line-break'> </span>that all previous votes incompatible with the provisions of said <span class='line-break'> </span>Code, or with the Act of Incorporation, shall be repealed, and that <span class='line-break'> </span>a copy of the new Code shall be printed with the next edition <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Catalogue. - -</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279281">
<h3><a name="page-1279281">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 114)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>114</p>
<p>The Code of By-Laws contains regulations <span class='line-break'> </span>for the most part additional to, or explanatory of, <span class='line-break'> </span>those contained in the act of Incorporation. -</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Art. 1 '> Art. 1 </span></p>
<p>Proprietors and Privileges.</p>
<p>A proprietor holding not less than three hundred <span class='line-break'> </span>feet of land is a member of the Corporation, and, as <span class='line-break'> </span>such, is entitled to vote at meetings and to hold a <span class='line-break'> </span>ticket admitting himself and his household to drive <span class='line-break'> </span>into the Cemetery.  A proprietor holding less than <span class='line-break'> </span>three hundred feet is entitled to hold a like ticket of <span class='line-break'> </span>admission, but has not the right of voting. -</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title=' Art. 2 '> Art. 2 </span></p>
<p>Meetings</p>
<p>The annual meeting of the Corporation shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>held in <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>, after due notification, on the first <span class='line-break'> </span>Monday in February, in the afternoon.  At this <span class='line-break'> </span>meeting the report of the Trustees for the preceding <span class='line-break'> </span>year shall be read, also the reports of the Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>and Superintendent.  The Trustees for the ensuing year <span class='line-break'> </span>shall be elected by ballot, and other business specified<span class='line-break'> </span>in the advertisement may be transacted.  If the <span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary neglect duly to call the Annual Meeting, <span class='line-break'> </span>a special meeting shall be called in the manner <span class='line-break'> </span>prescribed in the Act of Incorporation, and said spe- <span class='line-break'> </span>cial meeting shall be the annual meeting for the year <span class='line-break'> </span>in which it is held. - -</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279282">
<h3><a name="page-1279282">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 115)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>115</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 3'>Art. 3</span></p>
<p>Trustees and Officers</p>
<p>The first meeting of the Trustees shall be called <span class='line-break'> </span>by the Secretary, and be held within two weeks after <span class='line-break'> </span>the Annual Meeting of the Corporation.  At this <span class='line-break'> </span>meeting, there shall be chosen by ballot, a President, <span class='line-break'> </span>Secretary, Treasurer, a Committee on Finance, a <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Lots, a Committee on Grounds, and a <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Regulations and Records of Interments,<span class='line-break'> </span>for the ensuing year.  A Superintendent and</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='For amendt by addition see Mar. 2/57 p.169 April 6/57 p. 174_'>For amend<sup>t</sup> by addition see Mar. 2/57 p.169 April 6/57 p. 174_</span></p>
<p>Superintendent's Clerk, and a Gate-Keeper shall also <span class='line-break'> </span>be chosen by hand votes; and all salaries for the <span class='line-break'> </span>ensuing year shall be fixed.  The Trustees shall <span class='line-break'> </span>meet at least once a month, and five Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>shall constitute a quorum. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 4'>Art. 4</span></p>
<p>President</p>
<p>The President shall preside at meetings of the Cor<span class='line-break'></span>poration and of the Trustees; he shall fix the time <span class='line-break'> </span>and place for special meetings; he shall nominate<span class='line-break'> </span>all committees not otherwise provided for, and shall<span class='line-break'> </span>report in writing at the Annual Meeting the doings <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Trustees for the preceding year.  In the absence <span class='line-break'> </span>of the President, his place shall be supplied by a <span class='line-break'> </span>temporary Chairman. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 5'>Art. 5</span></p>
<p>Secretary.</p>
<p>The Secretary shall notify and attend all meetings, <span class='line-break'> </span>and shall record the doings of the Corporation and of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees.  He shall prepare and superintend the advertisements <span class='line-break'> </span>and other publicatons of the Trustees and Corporation. _</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279283">
<h3><a name="page-1279283">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 116)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>116</p>
<p>He shall prepare all legal instruments, and, shall <span class='line-break'> </span>give legal opinions on all subjects requried by the <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees.  He shall have charge of the delivery of tickets, <span class='line-break'> </span>of catalogues and other publications of the Trustees.<span class='line-break'> </span>He shall prepare, countersign and record in a <span class='line-break'> </span>book kept for the purpose, all deeds of conveyance of <span class='line-break'> </span>land in the Cemetery, and shall insert and keep in <span class='line-break'> </span>a portfolio all plans duly made of lots for proprietors, <span class='line-break'> </span>and shall number the same, and keep an index by <span class='line-break'> </span>which they may conveniently be found. ~</p>
<p>The Secretary shall receive such salary as the <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees may vote, together with the special fees des<span class='line-break'></span>ignated for services to  Proprietors. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 6'>Art. 6</span></p>
<p>Treasurer</p>
<p>The Treasurer shall give bonds in sum of three <span class='line-break'> </span>thousand dollars, for the faithful performance of the <span class='line-break'> </span>duties of his office.  He shall have custody of the funds<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation under the direction of the Trustees. _<span class='line-break'> </span>He shall collect dues, and pay bills approved by <span class='line-break'> </span>the President, or by the Chairman of any Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>duly authorizing an expenditure.  He shall keep the <span class='line-break'> </span>funds deposited in Bank to the credit of the Corporation,<span class='line-break'> </span>and draw the same as Treasurer.  He shall sign <span class='line-break'> </span>all conveyances.  He shall preserve and file all papers<span class='line-break'> </span>relating to his official duties, and shall report at the <span class='line-break'> </span>annual meeting, the receipts, and disbursements for the <span class='line-break'> </span>last year, and the existing state of the funds of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation.</p>
<p>The compensation of the Treasurer shall consist in a </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279284">
<h3><a name="page-1279284">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 117)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>117</p>
<p>Commission on sales to be fixed annually by the <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 7'>Art. 7</span></p>
<p>Superintendent</p>
<p>The Superintendent shall reside near the Cemetery, and, <span class='line-break'> </span>under the direction of the Trustees, shall have the general <span class='line-break'> </span>care and custody thereof: shall keep the avenues, <span class='line-break'> </span>paths and grounds in neat and satisfactory order; and, <span class='line-break'> </span>as agent for the Trustees, shall have the sole power to <span class='line-break'> </span>engage and discharge workmen on the ground, also to <span class='line-break'> </span>order and arrange their respective duties, and to pay their <span class='line-break'> </span>wages not otherwise provided for.  He shall see that the <span class='line-break'> </span>rights of the Corporation are respected by artists, mechanics <span class='line-break'> </span>and laborers employed on the ground by individual <span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors.  He shall see that all regulations with regard <span class='line-break'> </span>to interments, and the construction of tombs be duly com<span class='line-break'></span>plied with.  He shall fulfill all contracts made with <span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors for the repair of lots, and perform such other <span class='line-break'> </span>duties as the Trustees may require.  He shall have the <span class='line-break'> </span>power to remove from the Cemetery any improper and disorderly <span class='line-break'> </span>persons, also to abate nuisances and remove rubbish and<span class='line-break'> </span>unnecessary incumbrances.  He shall keep, in books pro<span class='line-break'></span>vided for the purpose, regular and accurate records of <span class='line-break'> </span>all interments, including the names and ages of persons <span class='line-break'> </span>interred, and the place and date of their interment:<span class='line-break'> </span>also of all monuments erected, and lots enclosed, sodded <span class='line-break'> </span>or otherwise improved; also of all monies received or dis<span class='line-break'></span>bursed by him, whether for wages, fees, improvement of lots, sales <span class='line-break'> </span>of wood or other articles, purchases made, or services rendered.<span class='line-break'> </span>On the first day of every month, or oftener if required,<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279285">
<h3><a name="page-1279285">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 118)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>118</p>
<p>by the Trustees, he shall render to the Treasurer copies <span class='line-break'> </span>of said accounts, with proper vouchers, and pay over<span class='line-break'> </span>to him all monies remaining in his hands.  The compen<span class='line-break'></span>sation of the Superintendent shall be a salary, and <span class='line-break'> </span>the use of a house, with no other perquisites. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 8'>Art. 8</span></p>
<p>Superintendent's Clerk</p>
<p>The Superintendent's Clerk shall assist the Superin<span class='line-break'></span>tendent by keeping the books, and performing such other <span class='line-break'> </span>duties as the Superintendent may require, and as are not <span class='line-break'> </span>incompatible with other duties required by the Trustees.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 9'>Art. 9</span></p>
<p>Gate Keeper</p>
<p>The Gate Keeper shall attend the Gate from sunrise to <span class='line-break'> </span>sunset every day in the week, and see to the enforce<span class='line-break'></span>ment of the rules respecting admittance. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 10'>Art. 10</span></p>
<p>Committees</p>
<p>Standing Committees shall be chosen by ballot; <span class='line-break'> </span>other Committees may be chosen by hand vote.<span class='line-break'> </span>Vacancies occurring in any Committee shall be filled <span class='line-break'> </span>in the same manner as that in which said Committee <span class='line-break'> </span>was chosen, and vacancies in the Standing Committees shall <span class='line-break'> </span>be filled at a meeting subsequent to that in which <span class='line-break'> </span>the vacancy is announced.  No Committee shall expend<span class='line-break'> </span>more than one hundred dollars on any one object, <span class='line-break'> </span>unless authorized so to do by vote of the Trustees. _</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279286">
<h3><a name="page-1279286">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 119)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>119</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 11'>Art. 11</span></p>
<p>Committee on Finance</p>
<p>The Committee on Finance shall consist of two Trus<span class='line-break'></span>tees.  They shall direct the Treasurer in regard <span class='line-break'> </span>to all sales and all investments of the funds of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation ^<sup>not otherwise provided for</sup>, or any part of the same.  They shall <span class='line-break'> </span>also act as Auditors, and shall examine the <span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer's accounts before each annual meeting, <span class='line-break'> </span>and satisfy themselves in regard to the correctness <span class='line-break'> </span>of said accounts, also in regard to the safe<span class='line-break'> </span>preservation of all evidences of property belonging <span class='line-break'> </span>to the Corporation; and they shall annex their <span class='line-break'> </span>report to the annual report of the Treasurer. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 12'>Art. 12</span></p>
<p>Committee on Lots.</p>
<p>The Committee on Lots shall consist of three Trustees.<span class='line-break'> </span>They shall have the general supervision of all sales, <span class='line-break'> </span>locations and enlargements of lots, also of all questions <span class='line-break'> </span>of right between individual proprietors, or between <span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors <s>or between proprietors</s> and the Corporation.<span class='line-break'> </span>No transfer or conveyance of land by the Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>shall take place until it has received the approval,<span class='line-break'> </span>in writing, of a majority of the Committee on Lots.  If an <span class='line-break'> </span>appeal to the Trustees is made by any party in interest, <span class='line-break'> </span>before the delivery of a deed, the Secretary shall delay <span class='line-break'> </span>acting until the case has been brought before the Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>and acted upon by them.  the Committee on Lots shall <span class='line-break'> </span>have power, subject to the concurrence of the Trustees, <span class='line-break'> </span>to contract with any proprietor for the repair of his <span class='line-break'> </span>lot perpetually, or for an indefinte time.  They shall, at least <span class='line-break'> </span>twice in each year inspect the lots which the Trustees have</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279287">
<h3><a name="page-1279287">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 120)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>120</p>
<p>undertaken to keep in repair, and see that the trust<span class='line-break'> </span>is duly executed.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 13'>Art. 13</span></p>
<p>Committee on Grounds</p>
<p>The Committee on Grounds shall consist of <span class='line-break'> </span>five Trustees.  They shall have general charge <span class='line-break'> </span>of the grounds, trees, avenues and paths in the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery, with power to make such alterations, repairs <span class='line-break'> </span>and improvements therein, as they shall deem ex<span class='line-break'></span>pedient.  But no avenues or paths shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>changed in situation, without the consent of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees expressed by vote. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 14'>Art. 14</span></p>
<p>Committee on Regulations and Records of Interments.</p>
<p>The Committee on Regulations and Records of Inter<span class='line-break'></span>ments shall consist of two Trustees.  They shall super<span class='line-break'></span>intend the general subject of Interments, and see<span class='line-break'> </span>that the laws of the Commonwealth, and those of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery, in relation thereto, be complied with.  They <span class='line-break'> </span>shall, from time to time, inspect the records and <span class='line-break'> </span>accounts of the Superintendent, and see that the same <span class='line-break'> </span>are suitably kept. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 15'>Art. 15</span></p>
<p>Interments.</p>
<p>No interment shall be made at Mount Auburn <span class='line-break'> </span>until such a permit as may be required by the laws <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Commonwealth, or of the City or town from which <span class='line-break'> </span>the deceased may be brought, together with an order from <span class='line-break'> </span>the proprietor of the lot in which such interment is to <span class='line-break'> </span>be made, or of his legal representative. _ shall have been</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279288">
<h3><a name="page-1279288">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 121)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>121</p>
<p>presented at the Gate: nor until the fees shall have <span class='line-break'> </span>been paid.</p>
<p>Until otherwise ordered, two dollars and fifty<span class='line-break'> </span>cents shall be charged for digging a grave and making <span class='line-break'> </span>an interment, and fifty cents additional for recording <span class='line-break'> </span>the same.  A deduction of one dollar shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>made from the above charges for a child under<span class='line-break'> </span>ten years of age.  For each interment in a tomb <span class='line-break'> </span>a charge shall be made by the Superintendent<span class='line-break'> </span>according to the amount of service rendered in the case.</p>
<p>The particulars and amounts of fees for burial <span class='line-break'> </span>shall be printed on the back of the order from the <span class='line-break'> </span>proprietor, together with the words, "payable at the time <span class='line-break'> </span>of interment. "</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 16'>Art. 16</span></p>
<p>Lots and Spaces. _</p>
<p>Lots shall be laid out by the Superintendent, <span class='line-break'> </span>subject to the approval of the Committee on Lots.</p>
<p>In all future sales of lots, a space of not less <span class='line-break'> </span>than three nor more than six feet in width, at the <span class='line-break'> </span>discretion of the Committee on Lots, shall be reserved <span class='line-break'> </span>between the fence limits of different lots, unless otherwise <span class='line-break'> </span>ordered by vote of the Trustees.</p>
<p>The land left vacant as intermediate space<span class='line-break'> </span>between lots in Mount Auburn, and not exceeding ten <span class='line-break'> </span>feet in width between any two lots may be sold to <span class='line-break'> </span>the nearest lot holder or holders, at one third of the <span class='line-break'> </span>selling prices per foot at the time of said sale, with <span class='line-break'> </span>the condition that said land shall forever be kept <span class='line-break'> </span>open and without interments: provided that, if the</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279289">
<h3><a name="page-1279289">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 122)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>122</p>
<p>Committee, on Lots deem it inexpedient in any <span class='line-break'> </span>special case to make such sale, the question may <span class='line-break'> </span>be submitted to the board of Trustees.</p>
<p>The price of a full lot, until otherwise <span class='line-break'> </span>ordered, shall be one hundred and fifty dollars, <span class='line-break'> </span>or fifty cents per square foot.  Enlarged lots, small <span class='line-break'> </span>lots, and land additional to lots, will be sold at a <span class='line-break'> </span>corresponding rate per foot.  Choice lots in such places <span class='line-break'> </span>as the Trustees may designate, will be held at an <span class='line-break'> </span>advanced price.</p>
<p>No lots shall be gratuitously conveyed to public <span class='line-break'> </span>bodies or private individuals. ~</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 17'>Art. 17</span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/61319' title='Public Lot'>Public Lots</a>.</p>
<p>Interments may be made in the <a href='/pages/subjects/61319' title='Public Lot'>public lots</a> be<span class='line-break'></span>longing to the Cemetery, and the graves numbered <span class='line-break'> </span>on stone, on payment of twelve dollars each, <span class='line-break'> </span>together with the customary fees payable in other <span class='line-break'> </span>cases of interment.  But no slab, monument or <span class='line-break'> </span>fence shall be erected upon or around said graves, <span class='line-break'> </span>without the approval of the Committee on Lots.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 18'>Art. 18</span></p>
<p>Sales and Conveyances</p>
<p>Lots applied for by purchasers shall be laid out <span class='line-break'> </span>by the Superintendent subject to the approval of the Committee <span class='line-break'> </span>on Lots.  If the sale is approved by a majority of said <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee, the purchaser shall then pay to the Treasurer <span class='line-break'> </span>the customary or stipulated price of the lot sold him,<span class='line-break'> </span>and the Secretary's fee of one dollar, and receive a cer<span class='line-break'></span>tificate therefor.  The Secretary, on receiving the Treasurer's</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279290">
<h3><a name="page-1279290">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 123)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>123</p>
<p>order for the deed of said lot, shall make record<span class='line-break'> </span>and return said deed to the Treasurer, who will deliver<span class='line-break'> </span>the same to the purchaser, upon his presenting the certificate <span class='line-break'> </span>and receipting for said deed.  In any doubtful case,<span class='line-break'> </span>the Secretary or Treasurer shall ask instruction from the <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees before executing a deed.</p>
<p>No deed of any lot shall be issued to more than <span class='line-break'> </span>one grantee: nor to any person as Trustee, Executor<span class='line-break'> </span>administrator, except by a vote of the Trustees, or the <span class='line-break'> </span>authority of the Committee on Lots.  No deed of any lot<span class='line-break'> </span>shall contain any special declaration of trust, without <span class='line-break'> </span>a vote of the Trustees therefor.</p>
<p>All deeds of conveyance by the Corporation shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>under the common seal, (which shall be that heretofore <span class='line-break'> </span>adopted.)  and signed by the Treasurer and countersigned<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Secretary, and recorded in the books of the Cor<span class='line-break'></span>poration.</p>
<p>One dollar shall be paid to the Secretary for recording <span class='line-break'> </span>any deed of transfer, and giving the due certificate of the same.</p>
<p>The forms of conveyance given in Appendix A. shall <span class='line-break'> </span>be used until otherwise ordered by the Trustees.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 19'>Art. 19</span></p>
<p>Lots of Deceased Proprietors.</p>
<p>When the devisee of a deceased proprietor of any lot <span class='line-break'> </span>in the Cemetery shall desire to place upon the Record<span class='line-break'> </span>of the deed of said lot, at the Secretary's office, the evidence <span class='line-break'> </span>of his title to the same, he may do so by producing a <span class='line-break'> </span>certified copy of the will of such proprietor, (if the title is <span class='line-break'> </span>deducible therefrom,) or of such portion of said will as <span class='line-break'> </span>relates to said title; and the same shall be duly</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279291">
<h3><a name="page-1279291">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 124)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>124</p>
<p>recorded in a book kept for that purpose, and <span class='line-break'> </span>proper reference thereto be made upon the margin <span class='line-break'> </span>of the original record. _</p>
<p>The Secretary shall receive the affidavit of <span class='line-break'> </span>any person who shall claim to be the sole heir <span class='line-break'> </span>at law of the deceased proprietor of any lot, in <span class='line-break'> </span>which the material facts necessary to support <span class='line-break'> </span>such claim shall be set forth, and he shall file <span class='line-break'> </span>the same with the papers of the Corporation, with <span class='line-break'> </span>proper reference thereto upon the margin of the <span class='line-break'> </span>original record. _</p>
<p>When the devisees or heirs at law of any de<span class='line-break'></span>ceased proprietor, or the Guardian or Trustees of such <span class='line-break'> </span>persons being infants, shall desire the appoint<span class='line-break'></span>ment of a person to represent the lot owned in <span class='line-break'> </span>common by them, written application to the Trustees <span class='line-break'> </span>shall be made by them in that behalf. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 20'>Art. 20</span></p>
<p>Plans and Portfolios. ~</p>
<p>A large map or plan of the Cemetery shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>kept at the Secretary's office, and a duplicate of the <span class='line-break'> </span>same at the Superintendent's office.  On these shall <span class='line-break'> </span>be entered, under the direction of the Committee on Lots, <span class='line-break'> </span>by a Surveyor to be from time to time designated <span class='line-break'> </span>by them, all avenues and paths duly named, <span class='line-break'> </span>and all lots sold or laid out by the Corporation, <span class='line-break'> </span>duly numbered.  If any avenue path or  lot shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>given up, altered or removed by the Trustees, a corres<span class='line-break'></span>ponding alteration shall be made in the Plan.</p>
<p>The Secretary shall procure and keep one or</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279292">
<h3><a name="page-1279292">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 125)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>125</p>
<p>more portfolios, in which he shall insert such <span class='line-break'> </span>plans as proprietors may respectively procure to be <span class='line-break'> </span>made of their lots, such plans to be drawn by a <span class='line-break'> </span>surveyor approved by the _____ on paper<span class='line-break'> </span>of uniform size, which shall be furnished by the Sec<span class='line-break'></span>retary, and no plans shall be introduced into <span class='line-break'> </span>the portfolio, unless they shall have been examined <span class='line-break'> </span>and approved by the Committee on Lots, or a majority <span class='line-break'> </span>of them, and certified by the Superintendent to be correct. <span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors shall pay the expense of their own plans, <span class='line-break'> </span>and one dollar to the Secretary for examining and introducing <span class='line-break'> </span>the same into the portfolio, and placing the name in the index.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 21'>Art. 21</span></p>
<p>Trees. _<span class='line-break'> </span>Trees standing within lots can be removed, if desired, by <span class='line-break'> </span>an application from the proprietor to the Superintendent, <span class='line-break'> </span>subject to the approval of the Committee on Grounds.  The <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Grounds have likewise charge of the general <span class='line-break'> </span>subject of introducing and cultivating, also of trimming <span class='line-break'> </span>and removing trees and shrubs in other parts of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 22'>Art. 22</span></p>
<p>Tombs</p>
<p>Lots for tombs may be sold in places approved by <span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees, and at prices fixed by them.  Such tombs <span class='line-break'> </span>shall be made in a strong, tight and durable manner, <span class='line-break'> </span>and every part, including the door, shall be at least <span class='line-break'> </span>one foot under ground. ~</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279293">
<h3><a name="page-1279293">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 126)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>126</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 23'>Art. 23</span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/57656' title='Receiving Tomb'>Receiving Tombs</a>. _</p>
<p>Bodies may be deposited in the <a href='/pages/subjects/57656' title='Receiving Tomb'>Receiving <span class='line-break'> </span>Tombs</a>, on payment of fifteen dollars to the <span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent.  But if, within four months after <span class='line-break'> </span>interment, the deposited body shall be removed to <span class='line-break'> </span>any part of Mount Auburn, ten dollars of the above <span class='line-break'> </span>sum shall be refunded, otherwise the whole fifteen <span class='line-break'> </span>dollars shall be forfeited to the Corporation; and the <span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent shall remove the body to such place <span class='line-break'> </span>as shall be directed by the Committee on Grounds.<span class='line-break'> </span>But the friends or relatives, with the consent of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Superintendent, and in a legal way, may, at their <span class='line-break'> </span>own expense, remove said body from the Cemetery.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 24'>Art. 24</span></p>
<p>Monuments, Stones, Fences, &amp;c.</p>
<p>Proprietors have the right to erect on their lots, fences <span class='line-break'> </span>monuments and stones of appropriate character. <span class='line-break'> </span>Wooden fences and gravestones of slate are not <span class='line-break'> </span>permitted.  Live hedges of small or moderate size <span class='line-break'> </span>are allowed. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 25'>Art. 25</span></p>
<p>Appropriations</p>
<p>No appropriations of money exceeding one thousand <span class='line-break'> </span>dollars for any one object, unless it be for the <span class='line-break'> </span>liquidation of a debt previously existing, shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>made by the Trustees except at a meeting at least <span class='line-break'> </span>seven days subsequent to the meeting in which the said <span class='line-break'> </span>appropriation had been moved; whereof special <span class='line-break'> </span>notice shall be given. ~</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279294">
<h3><a name="page-1279294">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 127)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>127</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art 26'>Art 26</span></p>
<p>Repair Fund</p>
<p>The Trustees will receive in trust from any <span class='line-break'> </span>proprietor a sum of money not less than one <span class='line-break'> </span>hundred dollars, the income of which shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>appropriated to the repair of his lot, according to <span class='line-break'> </span>the terms of trust given in Appendix B.</p>
<p>The Trustees may also guarantee the perpet<span class='line-break'></span>ual repair of lots, on the payment to the Treasurer<span class='line-break'> </span>of a sum not less than three hundred dollars, <span class='line-break'> </span>according to the terms of trust given in Appendix C. _<span class='line-break'> </span>In this case, if the Repair Fund should ever be <span class='line-break'> </span>lost, the whole property of the Corporation is held<span class='line-break'> </span>for the perpetual repair of such lots.</p>
<p>All monies received from proprietors for the <span class='line-break'> </span>purpose of keeping lots in repair, shall collectively con<span class='line-break'></span>stitute a separate fund to be called the "Repair Fund,"<span class='line-break'> </span>and shall be kept invested, under the direction of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Finance, in some public stock of this State, <span class='line-break'> </span>or of the National Government, or in the Stock of some<span class='line-break'> </span>Bank or Banks of this State, or in some personal notes or <span class='line-break'> </span>obligations of private persons, secured by a satisfactory <span class='line-break'> </span>collateral pledge or mortgage, on interest. _</p>
<p>Each lot, in relation to which such contract shall <span class='line-break'> </span>have been made, shall be credited in a book kept for <span class='line-break'> </span>the purpose, with the principal sum given on account <span class='line-break'> </span>of said lot, and, at the close of each year, a rateable <span class='line-break'> </span>proportion of the net income of the whole repair fund, <span class='line-break'> </span>less one half per cent, shall be carried to the credit <span class='line-break'> </span>of each lot, and the proper entries made <span class='line-break'> </span>accordingly. _</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279295">
<h3><a name="page-1279295">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 128)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>128</p>
<p>The Treasurer shall keep the Superintendent <span class='line-break'> </span>constantly informed as to all lots which the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation have agreed to keep in repair, <span class='line-break'> </span>and shall also state the sums paid by proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>as considration for such agreements.</p>
<p>A list of all the lots, the repair of which has <span class='line-break'> </span>been contracted for by the Corporation, shall be <span class='line-break'> </span>published in each edition of the Catalogue of <span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors, together with the names of the present <span class='line-break'> </span>owners, and the sums respectively paid on <span class='line-break'> </span>said lots.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 27'>Art. 27</span></p>
<p>Admittance</p>
<p>The Secretary shall furnish to each proprietor <span class='line-break'> </span>who may request it, a ticket entitling him and <span class='line-break'> </span>his household to drive with a carriage into the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery.  These tickets are not transferable.</p>
<p>In all cases where the Secretary is satisfied, <span class='line-break'> </span>by a written petition to the Trustees, that the heirs <span class='line-break'> </span>or devisees in common of any lot have agreed<span class='line-break'> </span>upon any one person to represent the same, he <span class='line-break'> </span>may issue the ticket for such lot to the person <span class='line-break'> </span>designated in such petition as representative <span class='line-break'> </span>of such lot, to remain good until the further <span class='line-break'> </span>action of the Board.  the petition, however, shall <span class='line-break'> </span>be presented, with notice of the Secretary's action, <span class='line-break'> </span>at the next meeting of the Trustees.</p>
<p>The Secretary is authorized to issue more than <span class='line-break'> </span>one ticket upon one lot, where he is satisfied that <span class='line-break'> </span>two or more persons are actual owners of a lot,</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279296">
<h3><a name="page-1279296">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 129)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>129</p>
<p>in fact, though the title is in the name of one only.</p>
<p>The Secretary is authorized to replace <span class='line-break'> </span>tickets which he is satisfied are actually lost.<span class='line-break'> </span>But if the lost ticket is found, the duplicate shall <span class='line-break'> </span>be returned to the Secretary.</p>
<p>Strangers from a distance, also persons having <span class='line-break'> </span>business in the Cemetery, may be admitted with <span class='line-break'> </span>carriages on presenting a note or ticket of admission <span class='line-break'> </span>signed by a Trustee, or by the Secretary or Treasurer.<span class='line-break'> </span>The Trustees, however, may, from time to time, pass<span class='line-break'> </span>such votes for the admission of strangers and other <span class='line-break'> </span>non-proprietors, and under such regulations, as they may <span class='line-break'> </span>deem expedient.</p>
<p>The public are, at present, allowed to walk into <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery except on Sundays and Holidays.  Persons<span class='line-break'> </span>having a relative or near friend interred there may enter <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery on Sundays and Holidays on presenting <span class='line-break'> </span>a card of admission from a Trustee, the Secretary <span class='line-break'> </span>or Treasurer.  All visitors are subject to the conditions <span class='line-break'> </span>and regulations prescribed in the Bye Laws. _</p>
<p>Teams, carts and heavy-loaded vehicles are not <span class='line-break'> </span>allowed to enter the front gate without the order of <span class='line-break'> </span>a Trustee.  No omnibuses are allowed to enter the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery.</p>
<p>The rules and regulations concerning visitors to <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery, shall be as given in Appendix D, until <span class='line-break'> </span>otherwise ordered by the Trustees. _</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279297">
<h3><a name="page-1279297">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 130)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>130</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 28'>Art. 28</span></p>
<p>Funerals</p>
<p>Early notice of funerals shall be given to the <span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent, on the ground at Mount Auburn. <span class='line-break'> </span>When a funeral arrives, a person will be in <span class='line-break'> </span>readiness at the gate to conduct the procession <span class='line-break'> </span>to the place of interment.  If military funerals <span class='line-break'> </span>on foot or on horseback  are admitted, no <span class='line-break'> </span>music, nor firing off of volleys will be allowed<span class='line-break'> </span>within the Cemetery.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Art. 29'>Art. 29</span></p>
<p>Alteration of By Laws.</p>
<p>No alterations shall be made in any of the <span class='line-break'> </span>By-Laws, unless the proposed alteration has been</p>
<p><b>Amended by words "addition" added, Mar 2<sup>d</sup> /57 p.170 _</b></p>
<p>submitted to the Trustees at a meeting [held ?] at <span class='line-break'> </span>least seven days previous to the meeting at <span class='line-break'> </span>which it is ^<sup>to be</sup> acted upon.</p>
<p>The following are the appendices referred to. - -</p>
<p>Appendix A. _</p>
<p>Form of conveyance of a Lot. _</p>
<p>Know all men by these presents.  That the <span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn, in con<span class='line-break'></span>sideration of ______ dollars paid to them by <span class='line-break'> </span>______ of ______, the receipt of which is hereby <span class='line-break'> </span>acknowledged, do hereby grant, bargain, sell and convey <span class='line-break'> </span>to the said _______ and _______ heirs and assigns,<span class='line-break'> </span>one lot of land in the Cemetery of Mount Auburn,</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279298">
<h3><a name="page-1279298">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 131)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>131</p>
<p>in the County of Middlesex, situated on the way <span class='line-break'> </span>called ______ and numbered on the <span class='line-break'> </span>plan of said Cemetery, _________ which plan <span class='line-break'> </span>is in possession of the said Corporation, for inspection <span class='line-break'> </span>by the said grantee, _______ heirs and assigns, <span class='line-break'> </span>at all seasonable times; the said lot of land <span class='line-break'> </span>containing _______ superficial square feet.</p>
<p>To have and to hold the aforegranted prem<span class='line-break'></span>ises unto the said ______ heirs and assigns,<span class='line-break'> </span>for ever; subject, however, to the conditions and lim<span class='line-break'></span>itations, and with the privileges following, to wit: _</p>
<p>First.  That the proprietor of said lot shall have the right to <span class='line-break'> </span>enclose the same with a wall or fence not exceeding one foot in <span class='line-break'> </span>thickness, which may be placed on the adjoining land of the Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration, exterior to the said lot; _</p>
<p>Second.  that the said lot of land shall not be used for <span class='line-break'> </span>any other purpose than as a place of burial for the dead; and no <span class='line-break'> </span>trees within the lot or border shall be cut down or destroyed, <span class='line-break'> </span>without the consent of the Trustees of the said Corporation;</p>
<p>Third.  That the proprietor of the said lot shall have the <span class='line-break'> </span>right to erect stones, monuments or sepulchral structures, and<span class='line-break'> </span>to cultivate trees, shrubs and plants in the same. _</p>
<p>Fourth.  the proprietor of the said lot <sup>of land</sup> shall erect, at his or her <span class='line-break'> </span>own expense, suitable landmarks of stone, or iron, at the corners <span class='line-break'> </span>thereof: and shall also cause the number thereof to be legibly <span class='line-break'> </span>and permanently marked on the premises.  And if the said pro<span class='line-break'></span>prietor shall omit, for thirty days after notice, to erect such <span class='line-break'> </span>landmarks, and mark the number, the Trustees shall have <span class='line-break'> </span>authority to case the same to be done at the expense of the <span class='line-break'> </span>said proprietor. _ <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279299">
<h3><a name="page-1279299">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 132)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>132</p>
<p>Fifth.  That if the landmarks and boundaries of the said <span class='line-break'> </span>lot shall be effaced, so that the said lot cannot, with <span class='line-break'> </span>reasonable diligence, be found and identified, the said Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>shall set off to the said grantee ______ heirs or assigns, <span class='line-break'> </span>a lot in lieu thereof, in such part of the Cemetery as they <span class='line-break'> </span>see fit, and the lot hereby granted shall, in such case, <span class='line-break'> </span>revert to the Corporation;</p>
<p>Sixth.  That if any trees or shrubs situated in said <span class='line-break'> </span>lot of land shall, by means of their roots, branches, or otherwise,<span class='line-break'> </span>become detrimental to the adjacent lots or avenues, or dangerous <span class='line-break'> </span>or inconvenient to passengers, it shall be the duty of the said <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, for the time being, and they shall have the right to <span class='line-break'> </span>enter into the said lot and remove the said trees and <span class='line-break'> </span>shrubs or such parts thereof as are thus detrimental, <span class='line-break'> </span>dangerous or inconvenient:</p>
<p>Seventh.  That if any monument or effigy, or any <span class='line-break'> </span>structure whatever, or any inscription be placed in or <span class='line-break'> </span>upon said land, which shall be determined by <span class='line-break'> </span>the major part of the said Trustees for the time being, <span class='line-break'> </span>to be offensive or improper, the said Trustees, or the major<span class='line-break'> </span>part of them, shall have the right, and it shall be their <span class='line-break'> </span>duty to enter upon said land, and remove the said offen<span class='line-break'></span>sive or improper object or objects. _</p>
<p>Eighth.  No fence shall from time to time, or at any <span class='line-break'> </span>time, be placed or erected in or around the said lot, the <span class='line-break'> </span>materials and design of which shall not first have been <span class='line-break'> </span>approved by the trustees, or a Committee of them. _</p>
<p>Ninth.  No tomb shall be constructed within the bounds <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Cemetery, except in or upon the lots situated in such parts <span class='line-break'> </span>of the grounds, as shall be designated by the Trustees for that purpose;</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279300">
<h3><a name="page-1279300">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 133)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>133</p>
<p>and no proprietor shall suffer the remains of any person<span class='line-break'> </span>to be deposited in a tomb or so authorized, for hire.</p>
<p>Tenth.  The said lot of land shall be holden <span class='line-break'> </span>subject to the provisions contained in an Act of the General <span class='line-break'> </span>Court, dated March 31. 1835. and entitled "An Act <span class='line-break'> </span>to incorporate the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn."</p>
<p>And the said Proprietors of the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery of Mount Auburn do hereby covenant to and <span class='line-break'> </span>with the said _____ heirs and assigns, <span class='line-break'> </span>that they are lawfully seized of the aforegranted prem<span class='line-break'></span>ises, and of the ways leading to the same from the <span class='line-break'> </span>highway, in fee simple; that they are free from all <span class='line-break'> </span>incumbrances; that the Corporation have a right  to sell <span class='line-break'> </span>and convey the said premises to the said _______<span class='line-break'> </span>______ for the purposes above expressed; and <span class='line-break'> </span>that they will warrant and defend the same unto <span class='line-break'> </span>the said ______ heirs and assigns forever.</p>
<p>In testimony whereof, the said Proprietors of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery of Mount Auburn have caused this <span class='line-break'> </span>instrument to be signed by their Treasurer, and <span class='line-break'> </span>countersigned by their Secretary, and their common seal to <span class='line-break'> </span>be hereto affixed, the _______ day of _________ in the <span class='line-break'> </span>year of our Lord, one thousand eight hundred and <span class='line-break'> </span>fifty.</p>

<p>Secondly. _ To suffer the surplus, if any, of such <span class='line-break'> </span>income or interest to accumulate, for such time as the <span class='line-break'> </span>^<sup>said</sup> Trustees may deem expedient, or in their discretion to <span class='line-break'> </span>apply the same surplus, or any part thereof, from time <span class='line-break'> </span>to time, to the <sub>*</sub><u>ornament</u> and preservation of the grounds <span class='line-break'> </span>of the said Cemetery, or to any other, or all the purposes</p>

<p>to which, by the Act of Incorporation, the funds of the said<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation may be lawfully applied, and which are <span class='line-break'> </span>appropriate to the objects of the establishment of the said <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery.</p>

" ~<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>_____</th> <th>} Committee <span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>_____</td> <td>} on Lots.</td> </tr> <tr><td>_____</td> <td>} A. D. 18 . . "</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> -------------------------------</p>
<p>Appendix D. <span class='line-break'> </span>Regulations concerning Visitors to the Cemetery.</p>
<p>The gates are opened at sunrise, and closed at sunset.</p>
<p>No money is to be paid to the Gate-Keeper. _</p>
<p>No persons are admitted on Sundays or Holidays, except<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors and members of their Household, and persons<span class='line-break'> </span>accompanying them. _</p>
<p>No refreshments, and no party carrying refreshments, will <span class='line-break'> </span>be admitted to come within the grounds at Mount Auburn.</p>
<p>All persons who shall be found within the grounds making <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279306">
<h3><a name="page-1279306">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 139)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>139</p>
<p>unseemly noises, or otherwise conducting themselves unsuitably <span class='line-break'> </span>to the purposes to which the grounds are devoted, will <span class='line-break'> </span>be required instantly to leave the grounds, and upon refusal,<span class='line-break'> </span>will be compelled to do so; such persons will also be <span class='line-break'> </span>prosecuted.</p>
<p>No vehicle is to be driven in the Cemetery <u>at a rate <span class='line-break'> </span>faster than a walk</u>.</p>
<p>No horse is to be left unfastened without a keeper.</p>
<p>No horse is to be fastened, except at the posts provided <span class='line-break'> </span>for this  purpose. _</p>
<p>All persons are prohibited from gathering any flowers, <span class='line-break'> </span>either wild or cultivated, or breaking any tree shrub or plant.</p>
<p>Any person who shall be found in possession of flowers <span class='line-break'> </span>or shrubs, while in the grounds, or before leaving them, will <span class='line-break'> </span>be deemed to have unlawfully taken them in the grounds, <span class='line-break'> </span>and will be prosecuted accordingly.</p>
<p>N. B. Persons carrying flowers <u>into</u> the Cemetery to be placed <span class='line-break'> </span>on any lot or grave, as offerings or memorials, are requested to <span class='line-break'> </span>notify the Gate-keeper, as they pass in; in every other case flowers <span class='line-break'> </span>brought to the Cemetery <u>must be left without the Gate, or with <span class='line-break'> </span>the Gate-keeper</u>, until the owner passes out again. _</p>
<p>All persons are prohibited from writing upon, defacing<span class='line-break'> </span>and injuring any monuments, fence or other structure, in or <span class='line-break'> </span>belonging to the Cemetery.</p>
<p>All persons are prohibited from discharging fire-arms <span class='line-break'> </span>in the Cemetery. _</p>
<p>The Superintendent, the Gatekeeper and any other <span class='line-break'> </span>person acting under them, shall have a right to require his or <span class='line-break'> </span>her name from any person other than a Proprietor, or a member <span class='line-break'> </span>of his family who shall visit the grounds, and upon his <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279307">
<h3><a name="page-1279307">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 140)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>140</p>
<p>or refusal, or giving a false name, to exclude <span class='line-break'> </span>them from the grounds. _</p>
<p>The Superintendent, the Gate-keeper, and all other <span class='line-break'> </span>persons acting under them, shall have full author<span class='line-break'></span>ity to carry thse regulations into effect, and shall <span class='line-break'> </span>give notice of any violations thereof to the Trustees.</p>
<p>The Superintendent has the care of the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery, and is authorized to remove all those who <span class='line-break'> </span>violate these regulations or commit trespasses. _ <span class='line-break'> </span>Trespassers are also liable to be fined fifty dollars.</p>
<p>Twenty dollars reward is offered to any<span class='line-break'> </span>person who shall give information to the Trustees, <span class='line-break'> </span>which shall lead to the conviction of the  offender, <span class='line-break'> </span>of any trespass done by taking or plucking any <span class='line-break'> </span>flowers, shrubs or trees, within the grounds, or of<span class='line-break'> </span>otherwise injuring the grounds, or of any other offence<span class='line-break'> </span>against the Laws and regulations provided for the <span class='line-break'> </span>protection of the Cemeery, and the monuments and <span class='line-break'> </span>erections therein. ~ <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279308">
<h3><a name="page-1279308">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 141)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>141</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees January 5, 1857_'>Trustees <date when='1854-01-05'>January 5, 1857</date>_</span></p>
<p>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees was <span class='line-break'> </span>held at the usual place on <date when='1857-01-05T10:00:00'>Monday January 5<sup>th</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>A.D. 1857. at 10 o'clock A.M.</date> --</p>
<p>There were present, <a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->the President</a>, Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/62841' title='Cheever, James'>Cheever</a>, <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/62842' title='Crocker, Uriel'>Crocker</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Curtis</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54772' title='Gould, Benjamin A. (1787-1859)'>Gould</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/104060' title='Lawrence, William R. (1812-1885)'>Lawrence</a><a href='/pages/subjects/54774' title='Little, Charles C.'>, Little,</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/54820' title='Nazro, Charles G.'>Nazro</a><span class='line-break'> </span>and <a href='/pages/subjects/54770' title='Read, James'><!--James-->Read</a>. - -</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='By-Laws reconsidered_ and'>By-Laws reconsidered_ and</span></p>
<p>This being the meeting next after the meeting at which <span class='line-break'> </span>the By-Laws were adopted, it was unanimously</p>
<p>Voted that the same be reconsidered: _<span class='line-break'> </span>and thereupon it was proposed that Article 15<sup>th</sup> which <span class='line-break'> </span>relates to "Inerments," should be so amended, as to require <span class='line-break'> </span>an order from the proprietor of a lot or his legal representative<span class='line-break'> </span>to be presented at thet Gate prior to an interment in said<span class='line-break'> </span>lot: _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Amended_ and'>Amended_ and</span></p>
<p>that the last article relating to "Alteration of By-Laws" should <span class='line-break'> </span>be amended as to require any Amendment to be proposed <span class='line-break'> </span>at a meeting seven days at least prior to the meeting at which <span class='line-break'> </span>the same should be passed: _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Adopted as a whole _'>Adopted as a whole _</span></p>
<p>And that a new Article entitled ' "Lots of deceased<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors" _ should be inserted immediately after Art. 18_<span class='line-break'> </span>and that the articles from that to the end should be <span class='line-break'> </span>renumbered.</p>
<p>Voted that the foregoing amendments be adopted, &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>the Code as amended be passed. _</p>
<p>Voted that the same be recorded in their order <span class='line-break'> </span>with the By-Laws as adopted at the last meeting, if space</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1279309">
<h3><a name="page-1279309">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 142)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>142</p>
<p>shall have been left for that purpose <small>in</small> said By Laws<span class='line-break'> </span>having been recorded on preceding pages. ~</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Committee on Permanent Fund report_ adopted_'>Committee on Permanent Fund report_ adopted_</span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Mr Curtis</a> of the Committee appointed in April <span class='line-break'> </span>last to consider and report upon a plan for raising a <span class='line-break'> </span>permanent fund for the repair and preservation of the <span class='line-break'> </span>grounds at Mount Auburn, submitted a report in <span class='line-break'> </span>writing of which the following is a copy: ~ and, after <span class='line-break'> </span>being discussed the same was adopted, and it <span class='line-break'> </span>was ordered that it be placed upon record. ~</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Copy of Report'>Copy of Report</span></p>
<p>"The Committee to whom, in April last, was referred<span class='line-break'> </span>the duty, to mature and report a plan for establishing <span class='line-break'> </span>an accumulating fund for the perpetual repair and <span class='line-break'> </span>preservation of the Cemetery _ have considered the said <span class='line-break'> </span>subject, and a majority of them ask leave to report _<span class='line-break'> </span>that, in their opinion, it is meet and proper that <span class='line-break'> </span>such a Fund should be created and held for those <span class='line-break'> </span>purposes. _ Up to the present time, the expenses of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery, of all kinds, have been defrayed by the proceeds <span class='line-break'> </span>of the sales of lots; โ This source of revenue must,<span class='line-break'> </span>sooner or later, cease to exist; and, inasmuch as there <span class='line-break'> </span>is no authority in the Charter for imposing assessments on <span class='line-break'> </span>the Proprietors, the time must inevitably arrive, when, if <span class='line-break'> </span>some such measure s the Com<sup>ee</sup> propose, be not adopted,<span class='line-break'> </span>the Company will be without the means of discharging their <span class='line-break'> </span>ordinary expenses. _ Your Committee cannot believe that this <span class='line-break'> </span>would be a wise policy. _ It would partake too much of the <span class='line-break'> </span>character of the youth who uses up his capital without making <span class='line-break'> </span>provision for his old age. _ Your Committee have obtained</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279310">
<h3><a name="page-1279310">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 143)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>143</p>
<p>from the Treasurer a statement of the product of sales <span class='line-break'> </span>of land from 1847 to1855 inclusive _ say nine years _ <span class='line-break'> </span>amounting to one hundred and fifty seven thousand <span class='line-break'> </span>three hundred and one dollars ($157.301) to which add <span class='line-break'> </span>the estimated amount of sales in 1856, say nineteen<span class='line-break'> </span>thousand dollars, making the aggregate for the preceding <span class='line-break'> </span>ten years of one hundred and seventy five thousand three<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred and one dollars, or seventeen thousand five hun<span class='line-break'></span>dred and thirty dollars a year on an average: _</p>
<p>For the last four years, the average is twenty two <span class='line-break'> </span>thousand five hundred and fifty five dollars a year.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Permanent Fund Continued'>Permanent Fund Continued</span></p>
<p>During the same period of time _ say ten years, <span class='line-break'> </span>the average of ordinary expenses of the Corporation,<span class='line-break'> </span>has been as near six thousand dollars as the Treasurer <span class='line-break'> </span>could compute it without a minute and unnecessarily <span class='line-break'> </span>exact examination of the accounts.  On the same principles <span class='line-break'> </span>the average for the last four years is nine thousand <span class='line-break'> </span>three hundred and seventy five dollars a year.  Each <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustee can form as good a judgment of the future <span class='line-break'> </span>prospects of the Company in regard to the product of sales, <span class='line-break'> </span>as the Committee can: but the Committee suppose<span class='line-break'> </span>that for some years to come, the sales will not be <span class='line-break'> </span>less than they have been during the year 1856, but will <span class='line-break'> </span>be more.  If this estimate be well founded, and the <span class='line-break'> </span>ordinary expenses do not exceed ten thousand dollars a <span class='line-break'> </span>year, there will be in the Treasury a balance of ten <span class='line-break'> </span>or eleven thousand dollars, to be applied to the discharge <span class='line-break'> </span>of the debts of the Corporation, and any other extraordinary <span class='line-break'> </span>expenditures.</p>
<p>The present debts, including the mortgage for <a href='/pages/subjects/53229' title='Stone Farm'>the Stone<!--farm--></a></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279311">
<h3><a name="page-1279311">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 144)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>144</p>
<p>Farm, do not exceed twenty two thousand dollars, <span class='line-break'> </span>and these are not in the hands of <a href='/pages/subjects/54274' title='Bond, George William'><!--Bond-->the Treasurer</a>, <span class='line-break'> </span>Bank and other shares, the market value of which <span class='line-break'> </span>is nineteen thousand dollars.</p>
<p>It will be born in mind that your Committee <span class='line-break'> </span>have taken no notice of the income received by the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation from Stocks or other sources, for defraying <span class='line-break'> </span>current expenss; they are desirous of confirming their <span class='line-break'> </span>views entirely to the probably produce from the sales <span class='line-break'> </span>of land as a means of establishing an accumulating <span class='line-break'> </span>Fund. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Permanent Fund Continued'>Permanent Fund Continued</span></p>
<p>Your Committee from these premises have come <span class='line-break'> </span>to the conclusion that the Trustees may, with safety, <span class='line-break'> </span>set aside every year, not less than one fifth part <span class='line-break'> </span>of the  gross proceeds of the sales of lots, for the purpose <span class='line-break'> </span>aforesaid: _ and as there is no institution <u>appa<span class='line-break'></span>rently</u> so well protected from the vicissitudes of trade, <span class='line-break'> </span>as the <a href='/pages/subjects/64235' title='Massachusetts Hospital Life Insurance Company'>Massachusetts Hospital Life Insurance Com<span class='line-break'></span>pany</a>, _ the Committee recommend that out of the <span class='line-break'> </span>proceeds of sales of lots in 1857, the above propor<span class='line-break'></span>tion thereof, be deposited by the Treasurer, with the <span class='line-break'> </span>said Company, provided that the Trustees for the <span class='line-break'> </span>time being, shall deem the same to be safe, upon the <span class='line-break'> </span>principle of accumulation, for the term of twenty years;<span class='line-break'> </span>And that he annually deposit the same proportion <span class='line-break'> </span>with said Company upon the same principle, only dimin<span class='line-break'></span>ishing the period annually, so that all the deposits may <span class='line-break'> </span>become payable at the same time. _</p>
<p>Your Committee have not calculated the amount <span class='line-break'> </span>of interest which would have accrued at the end of</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279312">
<h3><a name="page-1279312">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 145)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>145</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Permanent Fund Continued.'>Permanent Fund Continued.</span></p>
<p>twenty years; but they presume that, compounded<span class='line-break'> </span>as it would be annually, it would not fall much<span class='line-break'> </span>short, if any, of the amount of Capital deposited.<span class='line-break'> </span>At the expiration of that period; the Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>would be possessed of a Capital of nearly two<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred thousand dollars, the income of which <span class='line-break'> </span>would probably defray the current expenses.  If <span class='line-break'> </span>however our successors should find that the cur<span class='line-break'></span>rent expenses increase so considerably as to excite <span class='line-break'> </span>their apprehensions that the income of two hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>thousand dollars would be insufficient, they will<span class='line-break'> </span>undoubtedly take seasonable measures to enlarge <span class='line-break'> </span>the Capital, by increasing the annual deposits</p>

<p>Voted,, that any person who shall <span class='line-break'> </span>be designated by any Company, Society or Association, <span class='line-break'> </span>whether corporate or incorporate, which may own a lot of <span class='line-break'> </span>three hundred feet or more in the Cemetery of Mount <span class='line-break'> </span>Auburn, be hereby authorized to represent said lot, <span class='line-break'> </span>and vote at meetings of the Corporation. _</p>

<h3><a name="page-1279318">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 151)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>151</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Lot 747 &amp; 748 united in one under no. 747.'><a href='/pages/subjects/64656' title='Lot 747'>Lot 747</a> &amp; <a href='/pages/subjects/74939' title='Lot 748'><!--lot-->748</a> united in one under no. 747.</span></p>
<p>A memorial was presented in behalf of <a href='/pages/subjects/79960' title='Peterson, Fredrick A.'>Mr F. A. <span class='line-break'> </span>Peterson</a>, proprietor of <a href='/pages/subjects/64656' title='Lot 747'>lots 747</a>, &amp; <a href='/pages/subjects/74939' title='Lot 748'><!--lot-->748</a> situated upon <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/61224' title='Locust Avenue'>Locust Avenue</a>, each containing one hundred &amp; fifty<span class='line-break'> </span>square feet, both being in one enclosure with one tomb in common, <span class='line-break'> </span>that said lots may be united in one, making three <span class='line-break'> </span>hundred feet, under the <a href='/pages/subjects/64656' title='Lot 747'>number 747</a> &amp; thus constituting <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/79960' title='Peterson, Fredrick A.'>Mr Peterson</a> a member of the Corporation: _</p>
<p>After consideration it was voted that the prayer<span class='line-break'> </span>of the petitioner be granted. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Stone Farm _ as to right of Mass. Hort. Soc. in same _'><a href='/pages/subjects/53229' title='Stone Farm'>Stone Farm</a> _ as to right of <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Mass. Hort. Soc.</a> in same _</span></p>
<p>Upon Motion of <a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Mr Curtis</a>,,</p>
<p>Voted that the subject of the relations of this Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>to the <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Massachusetts Horticultural Society</a> in reference to the <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/53229' title='Stone Farm'>Stone Farm</a> be referred to the next Board of Trustees. _</p>
<p>The following special committees which had not before <span class='line-break'> </span>formally reported upon matters committed to them now either reported, <span class='line-break'> </span>or stated that they were not prepared to report, and were severally discharged. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee on Catalogue report progress'>Com<sup>ee</sup> on Catalogue report progress</span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/62842' title='Crocker, Uriel'>Mr Crocker</a> for the Committee to prepare &amp; publish <span class='line-break'> </span>the catalogue reported that the same was making progress and <span class='line-break'> </span>would probably be issued in a few weeks. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee to change position of Lot 598'>Com<sup>ee</sup> to change position of <a href='/pages/subjects/62819' title='Lot 598'>Lot 598</a></span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee to build Supts house'>Com<sup>ee</sup> to build <a href='/pages/subjects/57665' title='Superintendent&apos;s House'>Supt<sup>s</sup> house</a></span></p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Proprietors - February 2d 1857.'>Proprietors - <date when='1857-02-02'>February 2<sup>d</sup> 1857</date>.</span></p>
<p>Mount Auburn Cemetery</p>
<p>The annual meeting of the Proprietors of the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery of Mount Auburn, will be held at the <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/62836' title='Meionaon, Tremont Temple'>Meionaon, Tremont Temple</a>, on <date when='1857-02-02T16:00:00'>Monday, the 2<sup>d</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>day of February at 4 O'clock. P.M.</date> to hear the reports <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Trustees, Treasurer and Superintendent; to choose <span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees for the ensuing year, and to act on any other <span class='line-break'> </span>business which may legally come before the meeting.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'>Austin J. Coolidge</a> ,, Secretary ,,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a> <date when='1857-01-24'>Jan. 24. 1857 </date></p>
<p>Pursuant to the foregoing notice which was published <span class='line-break'> </span>more than seven days before the time of meeting in the <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58551' title='Boston Daily Advertiser'>Boston Daily Advertiser</a> and in the <a href='/pages/subjects/62837' title='Boston Evening Transcript'>Boston Evening Trans<span class='line-break'></span>cript</a>, the Proprietors met at the time and place therein <span class='line-break'> </span>named. _</p>
<p>A quorum being in attendance the President <a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'>Dr Big<span class='line-break'></span>elow</a> took the chair. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Records read _'>Records read _</span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'><!--Coolidge-->The Secretary</a> read the records of the last Annual <span class='line-break'> </span>meeting.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Treasr Rept'>Treas<sup>r</sup> Rep<sup>t</sup></span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/54274' title='Bond, George William'><!--Bond-->The Treasurer</a> read his annual report, also that <span class='line-break'> </span>of the Superintendent, which are recorded on pages 160-163,</p>
</div>

<p>Voted, that a Committee of three be appointed <span class='line-break'> </span>by the Chair to receive, assort and count the votes;<span class='line-break'> </span>that the name of each proprietor be checked as his <span class='line-break'> </span>vote is deposited; that proprietors present in person <span class='line-break'> </span>vote before those present by proxy;  and that where <span class='line-break'> </span>two or more proxies are presented from the same party,<span class='line-break'> </span>regard be paid to the one bearing the latest date. _</p>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Secy protem. appointed -'>Sec<sup>y</sup> protem. appointed -</span></p>

<p>Voted that the polls be closed at ยผ before <span class='line-break'> </span>6 by the clock in the Hall. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Temporary Adjournt'>Temporary Adjourn<sup>t</sup></span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/60695' title='Brigham, William'>Mr Brigham</a>, Chairman of the Committee stated <span class='line-break'> </span>that some two hours must necessarily elapse before <span class='line-break'> </span>the counting of the votes could be completed; _ and <span class='line-break'> </span>on motion of <a href='/pages/subjects/80043' title='Plummer, Farnham'>Mr F. Plummer</a>, Voted that <span class='line-break'> </span>this meeting stand adjourned to this place at <span class='line-break'> </span>8 O'clock to hear the report of the Committee &amp;c. _</p>
<p>The meeting reassembled at 8 O'clock, the Presi<span class='line-break'></span>dent in the Chair. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Adjournt to next day -'>Adjourn<sup>t</sup> to next day -</span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/60695' title='Brigham, William'>Mr Brigham</a> of the Committee stated ^<sup>that</sup> a considerable <span class='line-break'> </span>further time would be requisite to enable the Committee <span class='line-break'> </span>to announce the result of the ballotting. _ Accordingly<span class='line-break'> </span>upon motion of <a href='/pages/subjects/64692' title='Chapman, D. R., Mr.'>Mr Chapman</a>,</p>
<p>The meeting was adjourned to the next day (Tuesday)<span class='line-break'> </span>at 4 O'clock P.M. at the same place. _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Adjourned meeting - Feby 3d &apos;57'>Adjourned meeting -<date when='1857-02-03'> Feb<sup>y</sup> 3<sup>d</sup> '57</date></span></p>
<p>Adjourned Meeting. _ <span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1857-02-03T16:00:00'>Tuesday February 3<sup>d</sup> 1857.</date> _</p>
<p>At the hour appointed the meeting reassembled, <a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->the <span class='line-break'> </span>President</a> in the Chair . _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee to receive &amp;c votes report _'>Com<sup>ee</sup> to receive &amp;c votes report _</span></p>
<p>The Secretary being detained a few minutes, <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/64692' title='Chapman, D. R., Mr.'>Mr D. R Chapman</a> was appointed Secretary pro tem</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/60695' title='Brigham, William'>Mr Brigham</a> for the Committee to receive, assort &amp; count</p>
</div>
