<p>261</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Trustees Nov. 1. 1858'>Trustees <date when='1858-11-01'>Nov. 1. 1858</date></span></p>
<p>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees was<span class='line-break'> </span>held at the usual place on <date when='1858-11-01T10:00:00'>Monday, November 1<sup>st</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>AD 1858, at 10 O'clock a.m.</date> ~</p>
<p>There were present, <a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->the President</a>, Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/65205' title='Andrews, William T.'>An<span class='line-break'></span>drews</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/62841' title='Cheever, James'>Cheever</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/62842' title='Crocker, Uriel'>Crocker</a>, ^<sup><a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Curtis</a></sup> <a href='/pages/subjects/54772' title='Gould, Benjamin A. (1787-1859)'>Gould</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54774' title='Little, Charles C.'><!--Charles-->Little</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54820' title='Nazro, Charles G.'>Nazro</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/54770' title='Read, James'><!--James-->Read</a> and <a href='/pages/subjects/65944' title='Sleeper, Jacob'>Sleeper</a>.</p>
<p>The record of the last meeting was read. ~</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Report of Comee on Lots _ '>Report of Com<sup>ee</sup> on Lots _ </span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Mr Curtis</a> for the Committee upon Lots submitted a<span class='line-break'> </span>report upon two subjects of inquiry made by <a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'><!--Mann-->the<span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent</a>: _</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Perpetl Care of  Small lots _'>Perpet<sup>l</sup> Care of  Small lots _</span></p>
<p>1<sup>st</sup> Whether the Trustees will contract with the owner<span class='line-break'> </span>of lots consisting of less than three hundred square feet, for<span class='line-break'> </span>the perpetual care and preservation thereof for less than<span class='line-break'> </span>three hundred dollars, which is the minimum sum now<span class='line-break'> </span>prescribed by the Trustees.</p>
<p>After explanation of this subject in the report, the follow<span class='line-break'></span>ing vote was proposed for adoption, which being in<span class='line-break'> </span>amendment of the a bye-law, lies over until another meeting.</p>
<p>"That the Trustees will guarantee the perpetual care<span class='line-break'> </span>and preservation of lots^<sup>containing</sup> less than three hundred square feet,<span class='line-break'> </span>for such sum not less than one hundred dollars for<span class='line-break'> </span>each lot, as may be agreed upon between them and the<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietor of such lot."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Public monuments'>Public monuments</span></p>
<p>The second subject of inquiry was _</p>
<p>Whether the Trustees will require a sum of money to<span class='line-break'> </span>be deposited by those who erect what may be called<span class='line-break'> </span>public monuments for their future care and preservation.</p>
<p>Upon this matter the report recommended the</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1279429">
<h3><a name="page-1279429">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 262)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>262</p>
<p>following vote, which was put and unanimously<span class='line-break'> </span>adopted by the Trustees. _</p>
<p>"That no lot shall be sold for the purpose<span class='line-break'> </span>of erecting thereon  a Public monument or memorial,<span class='line-break'> </span>unless the subscribers to such monument, shall pay to<span class='line-break'> </span>the Treasurer such sum of money as the Committee<span class='line-break'> </span>having charge of this subject shall consider to be necessary,<span class='line-break'> </span>and adequate to defray the expense of the perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care and preservation of such monument and its<span class='line-break'> </span>apurtinances."</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee of Conf. with Mass. Hort. Soc.'>Com<sup>ee</sup> of Conf. with <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Mass. Hort. Soc.</a></span></p>
<p>The Committee appointed to confer with a similar<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee of the <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Massachusetts Horticultural Society</a>, through<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->the President</a> reported that they had had one or two<span class='line-break'> </span>meetings, and made some progress, it was thought toward<span class='line-break'> </span>an amicable arrangement of all existing questions between<span class='line-break'> </span>the two Corporations. An interchange of opinion was had<span class='line-break'> </span>upon one or two points which might become a basis<span class='line-break'> </span>of adjustment, but no vote was taken.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Passageways _'>Passageways _</span></p>
<p>A communication received from <a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'><!--Mann-->the Superintendent</a>, inquiring<span class='line-break'> </span>whether parties purchasing the passageways adjoining their<span class='line-break'> </span>lots have or have not the privilege of improving<span class='line-break'> </span>and ornamenting the same, was read, and upon<span class='line-break'> </span>motion of <a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Mr Curtis</a>, was referred to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Lots. _</p>
<p>The meeting was then adjourned.<span class='line-break'> </span>Attest <a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'>Austin J. Coolidge</a></p>
</div>

<p>was read, and upon motion, was adopted.</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Comee of Conf. with Hort. Socy'>Com<sup>ee</sup> of Conf. with <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Hort. Soc<sup>y</sup></a></span></p>
<p>The President for the Committee appointed to con<span class='line-break'></span>fer with a similar Committee of the <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Massachusetts Hor<span class='line-break'></span>ticultural Society</a>, in relation to an amicable settlement<span class='line-break'> </span>of all questions pending between that Corporation and<span class='line-break'> </span>the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn, sub<span class='line-break'></span>mitted as their report a paper embracing terms<span class='line-break'> </span>of such settlement, which had been agreed to by the<span class='line-break'> </span>Conference Committee, and the same was read and <span class='line-break'> </span>explained.</p>
<p>After some discussion, it was upon motion of<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/67763' title='Tobey, Edward S.'>Mr Tobey</a>.</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1279431">
<h3><a name="page-1279431">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 264)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>264</p>
<p>Voted, that said paper be referred back<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Committee with instructions to obtain from<span class='line-break'> </span>the <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Horticultural Society</a> a declaration that nothing<span class='line-break'> </span>contained therein shall be so construed as to<span class='line-break'> </span>authorize the said <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Horticultural Society</a> to exer<span class='line-break'></span>cise any intervention or control over the acts<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn,<span class='line-break'> </span>or their officers, in the management, disposition,<span class='line-break'> </span>improvement or sale of any land which it is<span class='line-break'> </span>now proposed to annex, or which may here<span class='line-break'></span>after be annexed to the present cemetery, other<span class='line-break'> </span>than is now exercised in relation to the land<span class='line-break'> </span>received from said <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Massachusetts Horticultural<span class='line-break'> </span>Society</a> under the act of 1835 incorporating the<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn.</p>

<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->The President</a> from the Committee of Conference<span class='line-break'> </span>having reported the terms of adjustment agreed upon<span class='line-break'> </span>in behalf of the <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Massachusetts Horticultural Society</a>, upon<span class='line-break'> </span>the one hand, and of this Corporation upon the other,</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Indenture'>Indenture</span></p>
<p>in the form of an indenture in two parts, bearing date<span class='line-break'> </span>the <date when='1858-12-18'>18<sup>th</sup> day of December A.D. 1858</date>, the same was read</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='accepted _ and ratified _'>accepted _ and ratified _</span></p>
<p>and considered, and it was thereupon unanimously</p>
<p>Voted _ that said Indenture be accepted and<span class='line-break'> </span>adopted by this Corporation, and that the President, <a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'>Jacob<span class='line-break'> </span>Bigelow</a>, in behalf thereof, be authorized to execute the<span class='line-break'> </span>same, with the corporate seal, and to acknowledge said<span class='line-break'> </span>indenture in behalf of said Corporation and to exchange<span class='line-break'> </span>the same with the said <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Massachusetts Horticultural Society</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span>and it was further</p>
<p>Voted, that said indenture be recorded in the Reg<span class='line-break'></span>istry of Deeds for the County of Middlesex.</p>

<div id="page-1279433">
<h3><a name="page-1279433">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 266)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>266</p>
<p>submitted us the report of the sub-committee appointed<span class='line-break'> </span>to estimate the amount which will be due this Cor<span class='line-break'></span>poration from the <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Massachusetts Horticultural Society</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span>according to the provisions of the indenture just adopted,<span class='line-break'> </span>an account stating the several items of debit and credit,<span class='line-break'> </span>from which it appeared that the amount^<sup>which will be</sup> due from<span class='line-break'> </span>said <a href='/pages/subjects/54281' title='Massachusetts Horticultural Society'>Horticultural Society</a>, <date when='1859-01-01'>January 1, 1859</date> is<span class='line-break'> </span><u> nine</u> <u> thousand</u> <u>and</u> <u>eight</u> &amp; <u>49/100</u> <u>dollars.</u></p>
<p>Voted that said report be accepted and placed<span class='line-break'> </span>on file.</p>
<p>Upon motion by <a href='/pages/subjects/54770' title='Read, James'>Mr Read</a></p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Stone Farm Annexed.'><a href='/pages/subjects/53229' title='Stone Farm'>Stone Farm</a> Annexed.</span></p>
<p>Voted that all land owned by the Proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn, situated on the southerly<span class='line-break'> </span>side of their Cemetery be, and the same hereby are,<span class='line-break'> </span>annexed to said Cemetery, and made part thereof.</p>
<p>Voted that <a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'><!--Mann-->the Superintendent</a> be directed to cause<span class='line-break'> </span>one or more interments to be made on said lands,</p>
<p>Voted that <a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'><!--Coolidge-->the Secretary</a> be directed to send a<span class='line-break'> </span>copy of these votes to the Assessors of <a href='/pages/subjects/53204' title='Watertown, MA'>Watertown</a>.</p>
<p>The meeting was then adjourned.<span class='line-break'> </span>Attest <a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'>Austin J. Coolidge</a> Secretary.</p>

<div id="page-1279435">
<h3><a name="page-1279435">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 268)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>268</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Additional Appropriation for  Lots 661, 1080, 1081'>Additional Appropriation for  <a href='/pages/subjects/68568' title='Lot 661'>Lots 661</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/70103' title='Lot 1080'><!--lot-->1080</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/70104' title='Lot 1081'><!--lot-->1081</a></span></p>
<p>A letter from <a href='/pages/subjects/54952' title='Tisdale, Mace'>Mace Tisdale</a> Esq. addressed<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Trustees, _ in which he offered to add five<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred dollars to the amount which now stands<span class='line-break'> </span>to the credit of himself and <a href='/pages/subjects/62033' title='Hewins, Simmon K.'>S K. Hewins</a> in the Fund<span class='line-break'> </span>for Repairs, for the perpetual care and preservation of<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/68568' title='Lot 661'>lots 661</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/70103' title='Lot 1080'>1080</a> &amp; <a href='/pages/subjects/70104' title='Lot 1081'><!--lot-->1081</a>, and the ornamental grounds con<span class='line-break'></span>nected with the same, upon the trusts and for the pur<span class='line-break'></span>poses mentioned in said letter _ was read.</p>
<p>And it was thereupon</p>
<p>Voted that said sum be and is hereby accepted,<span class='line-break'> </span>upon the conditions and trusts contained in his<span class='line-break'> </span>said letter. [see copy of letter in Record of Donations &amp;c.]</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Conveyance to  Heirs at Law &amp; others'>Conveyance to  Heirs at Law &amp; others</span></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'><!--Coolidge-->The Secretary</a> stated that many cases of embarrassment<span class='line-break'> </span>had occurred, and were likely to occur frequently for the<span class='line-break'> </span>reason that the charter confers upon this Corporation no<span class='line-break'> </span>power to convey lots to the heirs at law and other persons<span class='line-break'> </span>taking the estate of any deceased person, to hold the same<span class='line-break'> </span>in common. It was therefore, upon motion by<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Mr Curtis</a>,</p>
<p>Voted that a Committee of three be chosen to apply<span class='line-break'> </span>to the General Court of this Commonwealth for an act<span class='line-break'> </span>in addition to the act incorporating the Proprietors of the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery of Mount Auburn, which shall authorize the con<span class='line-break'></span>veyance of lots by this Corporation to the heirs at law, executors,<span class='line-break'> </span>trustees or others who may be authorized under the will<span class='line-break'> </span>of any deceased person to hold the same in common<span class='line-break'> </span>in the same manner as other lots are held, subject how<span class='line-break'></span>ever to the operation of Article Eight in respect to the<span class='line-break'> </span>representation of lots of deceased proprietors.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>The regular monthly meeting of the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>was held at the usual place on<date when='1858-02-07T10:00:00'> Monday, Feb<span class='line-break'></span>ruary seventh, 1859, at 10 o'clock a.m.</date> _</p>
<p>There were present, <a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->the President</a>, Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/62841' title='Cheever, James'>Cheever</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/62842' title='Crocker, Uriel'>Crocker</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54773' title='Curtis, Charles P.'>Curtis</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54772' title='Gould, Benjamin A. (1787-1859)'>Gould</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54774' title='Little, Charles C.'><!--Charles-->Little</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54820' title='Nazro, Charles G.'>Nazro</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/54770' title='Read, James'><!--James-->Read</a> and<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/65944' title='Sleeper, Jacob'>Sleeper</a>.</p>
<p>"The Committee to whom was referred the vote of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors of the Cemetery of Mount Auburn, at their<span class='line-break'> </span>last Annual Meeting on the subject of the care of Lots,</p>
<p>Report</p>
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='Report on Vote of Props at last Annual Meeting _'>Report on Vote of Prop<sup>s</sup> at last Annual Meeting _</span></p>
<p>That the Trustees feel bound to receive with<span class='line-break'> </span>respectful attention all suggestions coming from the<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietors; but that it is impossible for them to keep <span class='line-break'> </span>in proper order an aggregate of nearly three thousand private<span class='line-break'> </span>lots, which number is constantly increasing; and at<span class='line-break'> </span>the same time to pay the necessary expenses of the Cemetery,<span class='line-break'> </span>without consuming more than their whole income, and frus<span class='line-break'></span>trating the purposes of the permanent fund, which they have<span class='line-break'> </span>covenanted with their new proprietors to increase and keep<span class='line-break'> </span>inviolate. Besides which, the Committee have doubts whether</p>

<p><a href='/pages/subjects/54820' title='Nazro, Charles G.'>Mr Nazro</a> presented the following: _<span class='line-break'> </span>"That information having been received that <span class='line-break'> </span>the land adjoining Mount Auburn on the westerly<span class='line-break'> </span>side is about to pass into other hands, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that it is contemplated by the <a href='/pages/subjects/63961' title='Cambridge Railroad'>Cambridge Horse<span class='line-break'> </span>Railroad</a> to purchase it, and remove their stables<span class='line-break'> </span>there, which is likely to prove a great detriment to<span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery; and also in view of the great pros<span class='line-break'></span>pective advantage which may be secured to the Cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery by the purchase of said land by the Trustees</p>

<h3><a name="page-1279440">Trustees Records, Vol. 2, 1854 (page 273)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>273</p>
<p>"MOUNT AUBURN CEMETERY.<span class='line-break'> </span>The Annual Meeting of the Proprietors of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery of Mount Auburn will be held in <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a><span class='line-break'> </span>at the new rooms of the Board of Trade, No 55, <span class='line-break'> </span>Merchants' Exchange, (entrance through the Reading Room)<span class='line-break'> </span>on <date when='1859-02-07T16:00:00'>Monday, the seventh day of February, at 4 o'clock,<span class='line-break'> </span>P.M.</date>, to hear the reports of the Trustees, Treasurer,<span class='line-break'> </span>and Superintendent; and to choose Trustees for the<span class='line-break'> </span>ensuing year.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'>Austin J. Coolidge</a>, Secretary.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>, <date when='1859-01-31'>January 31, 1859</date>."</p>
<p>Pursuant to the foregoing notice which was pub<span class='line-break'></span>lished more than seven days before the time of meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>in the <a href='/pages/subjects/68571' title='Boston Daily Journal'>Boston Daily Journal</a> ^<sup>advertiser</sup>, and several other<span class='line-break'> </span>newspapers in <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>, the Proprietors met at the<span class='line-break'> </span>time and place therein named.</p>
<p>A quorum being in attendance, the President,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'>Dr Jacob Bigelow</a> took the chair.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/53157' title='Coolidge, Austin J.'><!--Coolidge-->The Secretary</a> read the printed notification<span class='line-break'> </span>of the meeting, also the record of the last annual<span class='line-break'> </span>meeting.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52529' title='Bigelow, Jacob'><!--Bigelow-->The President</a> read the annual report of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees, in print.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/54274' title='Bond, George William'><!--Bond-->The Treasurer</a> read his annual report; also<span class='line-break'> </span>that of the Superintendent, also in print.</p>
<p>Upon motion of <a href='/pages/subjects/60332' title='Richardson, Jeffrey'>Mr Jeffrey Richardson</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span>it was voted that the reports be severally accepted.</p>
</div>

<p>Voted that a Committee of three be appointed<span class='line-break'> </span>by the chair to receive, assort and count the<span class='line-break'> </span>votes for trustees.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>277</p>
<p>This certifies that we have examined the books and accounts<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Treasurer of the Proprietors of Mount Auburn, for the year<span class='line-break'> </span>ending <date when='1858-12-31'>December 31, 1858</date>, and have found them correctly kept<span class='line-break'> </span>and properly balanced, with satisfactory vouchers for all pay<span class='line-break'></span>ments charged.</p>
<p>The Certificates of Stocks and other evidences of property<span class='line-break'> </span>were found in accordance with the statements in his accounts.</p>
